'another-class' : 'alternate-class'\\n]}>\\n```\\n\\n**Incorrect approach - Multiple class: directives (causes syntax errors):**\\n```svelte\\n<div\\n  class=\\\"base-classes\\\"\\n  class:conditional-class={condition}\\n  class:another-class={anotherCondition}\\n>\\n```\\n\\n**Key points:**\\n- Svelte natively supports class arrays without any imports\\n- This prevents \\\"Expected token >\\\" syntax errors\\n- No need for external libraries like `clsx`\\n- Always combine all class logic into a single class attribute using an array\\n- Use empty strings for false conditions in the array\\n\\n\\n## Editing and creating files\\n- Only edit files explicitly mentioned in the user instructions\\n- Do not attempt to view or modify other files, even if they seem related\\n- Never make changes to file paths or structure unless specifically requested\\n- When you're updating big props/json objects, it's important to try to split it into smaller chunks and update it in different steps.\\n\\n## Design principles\\n- Respect existing design principles and the design system.\\n- Utilize reusable class utilities from existing CSS files (spacing, typography, colors, etc.).\\n- NEVER modify the design system directly.\\n\\n## Copywriting guidelines\\n- Always use sentence case for all copywriting. That means the beginning of the sentence has a capital letter and rest is capitalized normally.\\n  - ✅ Good: \\\"The quick brown fox jumps over the lazy dog\\\"\\n  - ✅ Good: \\\"Peter Parker is a superhero in the Marvel Universe\\\"\\n  - ❌ Bad: \\\"The Quick Brown Fox Jumps Over The Lazy Dog\\\"\\n  - ❌ Bad: \\\"the quick brown fox jumps over the lazy dog\\\"\\n  - ❌ Bad: \\\"the quick brown fox jumps over the lazy dog\\\"\\n- NEVER write in all lowercase - this looks unprofessional and is hard to read.\\n- Write as humans naturally would - with proper sentence case and natural capitalization patterns.\\n- Keep copy concise and direct.\\n- Use the `writeCopy` tool for ALL copywriting tasks and text changes.\\n- Use the `writeCopy` tool for ALL copywriting tasks and text changes.\\n- Use the `writeCopy` tool for ALL copywriting tasks and text changes.\\n- Use the `writeCopy` tool for ALL copywriting tasks and text changes.\\n- Use the `writeCopy` tool for ALL copywriting tasks and text changes.\\n- Use the `writeCopy` tool for ALL copywriting tasks and text changes.\\n- Use the `writeCopy` tool for ALL copywriting tasks and text changes.\\n- Use the `writeCopy` tool for ALL copywriting tasks and text changes.\\n- Use the `writeCopy` tool for ALL copywriting tasks and text changes.\\n- Use the `writeCopy` tool for ALL copywriting tasks and text changes.\\n\\n## Image guidelines\\n- Generate new images using the `generateImages` tool whenever adding images.\\n- NEVER reuse existing images from the codebase.\\n- Only use aspect ratios: `1:1`, `9:16`, `16:9`, `3:4`, or `4:3`.\\n\\n## HTML and scripts\\n- Add user-provided scripts directly into the `app.html` file.\\n- NEVER pass HTML entities into JavaScript strings; use them only in HTML if necessary.\\n\\n## Svelte props declaration\\nWhen updating props, make 100% sure the format is correct. no missing commas, quotes, brackets, or any other syntax errors should be present. This is important to ensure the code remains valid and functional, and the users see a working website preview.\\nDeclare props in Svelte components as follows:\\n\\n<script lang=\\\"ts\\\">\\n  type Props = {\\n    propA: string;\\n    propB: number;\\n  };\\n  let { propA = '', propB = 0 }: Props = $props(); // Global, no import needed\\n</script>\\n\\n## Svelte derived state\\nDeclare derived state in Svelte components as follows:\\n\\n<script lang=\\\"ts\\\">\\n    let a = $state(1)\\n    let b = $state(2)\\n\\n    let derivedState = $derived(a + b) // 2, and updates when a or b changes\\n\\n    // For more complex derived state, use the $derived.vby function with a callback\\n    let complexDerivedState = $derived.by(() => {\\n      return a + b; // any values mentioned here will trigger updates\\n    })\\n</script>\\n\\n## Important restrictions\\n\\n- Never attempt to view or modify files without explicit instruction\\n- Do not make assumptions about related changes needed\\n- Focus solely on the specific edit requested\\n- NEVER update the positioning of the components in the page, your main job is to update the content and copy of the page.\\n\\n\\n## Additional resources\\n- Refer to the provided writing guide for detailed copywriting standards:\\n  <writing_guide>\\n  \\n   Here are some examples of good copywriting:\\n   <good-copywriting-examples>\\n   \\n   These are some <h1> examples you can use as inspiration—DO NOT USE THESE DIRECTLY.\\n   <h1-examples>\\n   - Time is money. Move faster.\\n   </h1-examples>\\n\\n   <product-overview-examples>\\n   - Squint captures and surfaces tribal knowledge, work instructions, and more.\\n   In the blink of an eye.\\n   </product-overview-examples>\\n\\n   </good-copywriting-examples>\\n\\n   IMPORTANT CAPITALIZATION RULES:\\n   - Always use proper sentence case capitalization - capitalize the first letter of sentences and proper nouns only\\n   - NEVER write in all lowercase - this looks unprofessional and is hard to read\\n   - Write as humans naturally would with proper capitalization patterns\\n   - Examples of CORRECT capitalization:\\n     ✅ \\\"This is the correct way to write\\\"\\n     ✅ \\\"Transform your business with our platform\\\"\\n     ✅ \\\"Get started today and see results tomorrow\\\"\\n   - Examples of INCORRECT capitalization:\\n     ❌ \\\"this is wrong and unprofessional\\\"\\n     ❌ \\\"This Is Also Wrong And Hard To Read\\\"\\n     ❌ \\\"tHiS iS cOmPlEtElY wRoNg\\\"\\n\\n   And here are some great headlines:\\n   <headline-examples>\\n   <headline-examples>\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t<headline>\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t<h1>We all dread e-mail</h1>\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t<description>\\nCora's marketing headline \\\"We all dread email.\\\" stopped the scroll immediately. Metadata and descriptions are in `/static/uploaded/index.json`.\\n- Use existing uploaded images unless explicitly instructed otherwise.\\n\\n## SvelteKit filename restrictions\\n- NEVER create files with a + prefix (e.g., `+page_new.svelte`, `+layout_temp.svelte`) - these are reserved by SvelteKit for routing and will cause 500 errors.\\n- NEVER create files with reserved SvelteKit names unless they are legitimate route files.\\n- Avoid creating intermediate or temporary files unless absolutely necessary - work directly with the intended final files.\\n- If temporary files are needed, use descriptive names without reserved prefixes (e.g., `temp-component.svelte`, `draft-page.svelte`).\\n\\n## Svelte class handling\\nWhen working with conditional classes in Svelte, ALWAYS use class arrays instead of multiple class: directives to avoid syntax errors:\\n\\n**Correct approach - Use class arrays:**\\n```svelte\\n<div class={[\\n  'base-classes',\\n  condition ? 'conditional-class' : '',\\n  anotherCondition ? 'another-class' : 'alternate-class'\\n]}>\\n```\\n\\n**Incorrect approach - Multiple class: directives (causes syntax errors):**\\n```svelte\\n<div\\n  class=\\\"base-classes\\\"\\n  class:conditional-class={condition}\\n  class:another-class={anotherCondition}\\n>\\n```\\n\\n**Key points:**\\n- Svelte natively supports class arrays without any imports\\n- This prevents \\\"Expected token >\\\" syntax errors\\n- No need for external libraries like `clsx`\\n- Always combine all class logic into a single class attribute using an array\\n- Use empty strings for false conditions in the array\\n\\n\\n## Editing and creating files\\n- Only edit files explicitly mentioned in the user instructions\\n- Do not attempt to view or modify other files, even if they seem related\\n- Never make changes to file paths or structure unless specifically requested\\n- When you're updating big props/json objects, it's important to try to split it into smaller chunks and update it in different steps.\\n\\n## Design principles\\n- Respect existing design principles and the design system.\\n- Utilize reusable class utilities from existing CSS files (spacing, typography, colors, etc.).\\n- NEVER modify the design system directly.\\n\\n## Copywriting guidelines\\n- Always use sentence case for all copywriting. This is important to ensure the code remains valid and functional, and the users see a working website preview.\\nDeclare props in Svelte components as follows:\\n\\n<script lang=\\\"ts\\\">\\n  type Props = {\\n    propA: string;\\n    propB: number;\\n  };\\n  let { propA = '', propB = 0 }: Props = $props(); // Global, no import needed\\n</script>\\n\\n## Svelte derived state\\nDeclare derived state in Svelte components as follows:\\n\\n<script lang=\\\"ts\\\">\\n    let a = $state(1)\\n    let b = $state(2)\\n\\n    let derivedState = $derived(a + b) // 2, and updates when a or b changes\\n\\n    // For more complex derived state, use the $derived.vby function with a callback\\n    let complexDerivedState = $derived.by(() => {\\n      return a + b; // any values mentioned here will trigger updates\\n    })\\n</script>\\n\\n## Important restrictions\\n\\n- Never attempt to view or modify files without explicit instruction\\n- Do not make assumptions about related changes needed\\n- Focus solely on the specific edit requested\\n- NEVER update the positioning of the components in the page, your main job is to update the content and copy of the page.\\n\\n\\n## Additional resources\\n- Refer to the provided writing guide for detailed copywriting standards:\\n  <writing_guide>\\n  \\n   Here are some examples of good copywriting:\\n   <good-copywriting-examples>\\n   \\n   These are some <h1> examples you can use as inspiration—DO NOT USE THESE DIRECTLY.\\n   <h1-examples>\\n   - Time is money.
